عالم
قادر
حي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is purely theological and not linguistic.
Correction: Baqillani's argument relies on Arabic grammatical patterns (elative forms) to derive ontological conclusions about divine attributes.

Checkpoint

A) The word 'qadir' is always used for God.
B) The elative form is possible for 'powerful' but not for 'living'.
C) Life has no opposite.
D) Power is always present in life.

Key Takeaway
The inability to use elative forms for a supposed attribute indicates that attribute is not separable from the essence.

?
The opponents could not say 'more living' because life is essential to their being. Is your faith an essential part of your identity, or just a quality you put on? What would change if you treated it as your very life?

The Multiplicity of Hypostases Beyond Three
Baqillani shows that accepting distinct attributes leads to more than three hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a series of conditional arguments to show that the Christian doctrine of three hypostases leads to an absurd multiplicity.

Core Idea
Accepting distinct attributes as hypostases leads to an indefinite number, not just three.

Baqillani now turns the Christians' own reasoning against them. If attributes like life, knowledge, will, etc. are distinct hypostases, then why stop at three? By applying their logic consistently, Baqillani forces the opponent into absurd conclusions. This passage is a masterclass in reductio ad absurdum within theological debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the flow. Then read the translation. Notice how Baqillani presents a series of conditional arguments.
The passage is short but dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the logical moves
The passage contains four distinct conditional objections. Try to list them: (1) If endurance is identical to essence, then life and knowledge also are; (2) If will and speech are acts, then knowledge is also an act; (3) If knowing without acting is allowed, then willing and speaking without acting is also allowed; (4) If hearing and sight are identical to knowledge, then knowledge is identical to life.
Each move is a 'if...then' that mirrors the Christian's own claims.
3
Understand the goal of each move
Each move aims to show that the Christians cannot consistently hold to three hypostases. The first move reduces to one, the second to two, the third allows many, and the fourth again leads to two.
The overall conclusion: no answer from the Christians.
4
Reflect on the method
Baqillani is using the principle of 'what applies to one applies to all' (qiyas). He takes a Christian statement and applies the same logic elsewhere to show inconsistency.
This is a common dialectical technique in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يقال لهم: ما أنكرتم أن تكون الأقانيم خمسة وعشرة؟ لأننا نقول: إن الباري موجود حي عالم قادر؛ ونقول: إنه مريد وباق وسميع وبصير ومتكلم؛ والباقي السميع البصير المتكلم المريد لا يكون كذلك إلا لوجود بقاء وإرادة وسمع وبصر وكلام. فإن قالوا البقاء هو هو، قيل لهم: والحياة والعلم هما هو؟ فقولوا إنه أقنوم واحد. فإن قالوا: الكلام والإرادة فعل من أفعال المتكلم المريد، قيل لهم: وكذلك العلم فعل من أفعال العالم؛ فقولوا: إنه أقنومان. فإن قالوا: قد يعلم بالعلم من لم يفعله، قيل لهم: وقد يريد بالإرادة ويتكلم بالكلام من لا يفعله؛ وكذلك إن قالوا سمع الباري وبصره هو نفس علمه فوجب أنهما ليسا باقنومين غير العلم قيل لهم: وكذلك علم الباري هو حياته فوجب أن يكون أقنومين؛ ولا جواب لهم عن شيء من ذلك.
And likewise it is said to them: what prevents you from saying the hypostases are five and ten? Because we say: the Creator is existent, living, knowing, powerful; and we say: He is willing, enduring, hearing, seeing, speaking; and the enduring, hearing, seeing, speaking, willing is not so except by the existence of endurance, will, hearing, sight, and speech. If they say endurance is identical [to essence], it is said to them: and life and knowledge are also identical? Then say it is one hypostasis. If they say speech and will are acts of the speaker and willer, it is said to them: likewise knowledge is an act of the knower; then say there are two hypostases. If they say one may know by knowledge without having performed it, it is said to them: and one may will by will and speak by speech without having performed it; and likewise if they say God's hearing and sight are identical to His knowledge, so they are necessarily not two hypostases other than knowledge, it is said to them: and likewise God's knowledge is His life, so it must be that they are two hypostases; and there is no answer for them concerning any of that.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step refutation showing that the Christian logic leads to an indefinite number of hypostases. Baqillani lists attributes: existence, life, knowledge, power, will, endurance, hearing, sight, speech. If the Christian claims that some attributes (like endurance) are identical to the essence, then the same should apply to life and knowledge, reducing to one hypostasis. If they claim will and speech are acts, then knowledge should also be an act, giving two hypostases. If they claim one can possess knowledge without having acted, then the same applies to will and speech. Finally, if they claim hearing and sight are identical to knowledge, then similarly knowledge is identical to life, leading to two hypostases. The argument traps the opponent in inconsistency, concluding they have no valid response.

Key Terms
أقنوم
بقاء
إرادة
سمع
بصر
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani is asserting that God has many distinct hypostases.
Correction: He is using the Christians' own reasoning to show it leads to absurd conclusions; he does not affirm multiple hypostases.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue would happen if Christians claim that will and speech are acts?
A) Then knowledge would also be an act, leading to two hypostases.
B) Then there would be five hypostases.
C) Then God would not be omnipotent.
D) Then life and knowledge would be identical.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the Christian logic of distinct attributes leads to an indefinite multiplicity of hypostases, thus undermining the doctrine of three.

Refuting the Christian Limitation of Hypostases
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim that hypostases are only for self-referential attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the Christian claim that hypostases are limited to self-referential attributes, showing it leads to an infinite number of hypostases and undermines the trinity.

Core Idea
If self-referential attributes define hypostases, then many more than three arise, breaking the trinity.

This passage presents a Christian counter-argument that hypostases only apply to attributes that relate to God Himself, such as existence, substance, life, and knowledge. Baqillani turns this logic against them, showing that other self-referential attributes like being eternal or enduring would also qualify, multiplying hypostases beyond three. This effectively refutes the Trinity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Christian claim
Read the first part where the Christian speaker defines hypostasis as only for self-referential attributes (existence, substance, life, knowledge). Note that they use these to justify exactly three hypostases.
2
Follow Baqillani's counter
Baqillani adds attributes like being eternal and being enduring, which are also self-referential. He asks: if these are hypostases too, then there would be more than three.
3
Understand the logical conclusion
The Christian position collapses because they cannot limit the number of self-referential attributes. Baqillani concludes that this argument abandons the trinity.
4
Reflect on the method
Notice Baqillani's dialectical method: he accepts the Christian definition but shows it leads to absurdity, thus refuting them without relying on Islamic premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال منهم قائل: الأقنومية إنما تثبت للباري بصفة إلى نفسه لا تعلق لها بغيره وهي كونه موجوداً وجوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه وكونه حيا يرجع إليه ولا تعلق له بغيره وكونه عالماً بنفسه صفة يرجع بها إلى نفسه وإنما له أقنوم بكونه عالماً بنفسه لا بغيره؛ قيل لهم: وكذلك هو قديم بنفسه وليس كل موجود جوهراً قديماً بنفسه؟ فوجب أن يكون كونه قديماً أقنوماً رابعاً؛ وكذلك كونه باقياً صفة هو شيء موجود بنفسه وجوهر بنفسه فيجب أن يكون كونه شيئاً موجوداً أقنوماً وكونه جوهراً أقنوماً لأنه ليس كل موجود جوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه لا تعلق له بغيره، وليس كل موجود باقياً، فيجب أن يكون كونه باقياً أقنوماً خامساً، ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك، وفيه ترك التثليث.
If a speaker among them says: hypostasis is only established for the Creator by an attribute relating to Himself, having no relation to other than Him, and it is His being existent and a substance referring to Himself, and His being living referring to Him, having no relation to other than Him, and His being knowing by Himself, an attribute by which He refers to Himself, and He only has a hypostasis by His being knowing by Himself, not by other than Him; it is said to them: and likewise He is eternal by Himself, and is every existent a substance eternal by Himself? So it must be that His being eternal is a fourth hypostasis; and likewise His being enduring is an attribute, He is something existent by Himself and a substance by Himself, so it must be that His being a thing existent is a hypostasis and His being a substance is a hypostasis, because not every existent is a substance referring to Himself, having no relation to other than Him, and not every existent is enduring, so it must be that His being enduring is a fifth hypostasis, and there is no answer for them concerning that, and in it is the abandonment of the trinity.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage presents a Christian counter-argument and its refutation. The Christian claims that hypostasis (aqnūm) is only applied to attributes that are self-referential (relating to God's essence, not to creation) such as existence, substance, life, and knowledge. Baqillani turns this against them: being eternal by Himself is also a self-referential attribute, so it should be a fourth hypostasis. Similarly, being a substance, being a thing, being enduring are all self-referential, adding a fifth, sixth, etc. This shows the arbitrary limitation to three hypostases is unsustainable. The final phrase 'and in it is the abandonment of the trinity' means the Christian position is refuted, effectively abandoning the trinity.

قديم
باق
جوهر
موجود

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani is affirming multiple hypostases in God.
Correction: Baqillani is not affirming that; he is using the Christian's own definition to show that it logically leads to many hypostases, which undermines their claim of exactly three.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue would follow from the Christian claim that hypostasis is only for self-referential attributes?
A) That there are exactly three hypostases.
B) That being eternal by itself would be a fourth hypostasis.
C) That only knowledge is a hypostasis.
D) That life is not a hypostasis.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Christian limitation of hypostases by showing that the same logic would produce many hypostases, thereby abandoning the trinity.

The Argument Against Three Hypostases
Baqillani refutes the Christian hypostasis doctrine by reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the Christian doctrine of three hypostases by demonstrating that the logic used to define them actually requires more than three, thereby abandoning the Trinity.

Core Idea
Christian hypostatic logic leads to more than three hypostases, not three.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani confronts the Christian claim that God has three hypostases (aqānīm) based on attributes like knowledge and life. He first presents their reasoning, then turns it against them by demonstrating that the same logic would require additional hypostases such as eternity and everlastingness. The result is an absurd multiplication that abandons the Trinity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Christian Claim
Read the Christian argument: hypostases are attributes that refer only to God's essence, such as being existent, substance, living, and knowledgeable. They claim God has a hypostasis for being knowledgeable by Himself.
This is the position Baqillani will refute.
2
Identify the Initial Comparison
Baqillani points out that if knowledge and life are both hypostases, then since God's knowledge is His life, the Christian would have to say God has two hypostases for these two attributes, but they already claim three total.
3
Follow the Refutation
Now apply the same criterion to other attributes: God is eternal by Himself, everlasting, a thing, and a substance. Each of these also refers only to His essence, so they would each be a separate hypostasis.
This shows the logic leads to at least five hypostases.
4
Realize the Conclusion
Since the Christian definition leads to more than three hypostases, the doctrine of the Trinity is abandoned. The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.
Baqillani concludes that they have no answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باقنومين غير العلم قيل لهم : وكذلك علم الباري سبحانه هو حياته فوجب أن يكون أقنومين ؛ ولا جواب لهم عن شيء من ذلك . فإن قال منهم قائل : الأقنومية إنما تثبت للباري بصفة إلى نفسه لا تعلق لها بغيره وهي كونه موجوداً وجوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه وكونه حيا يرجع إليه ولا تعلق له بغيره وكونه عالماً بنفسه صفة يرجع بها إلى نفسه ؛ وإنما له أقنوم بكونه عالماً بنفسه لا بغيره ؛ قيل لهم : وكذلك هو قديم بنفسه وليس كل موجود جوهراً قديماً بنفسه؟ فوجب أن يكون كونه قديماً أقنوماً رابعاً ؛ وكذلك كونه باقياً صفة هو . هو شيء موجود بنفسه وجوهر بنفسه فيجب أن يكون كونه شيئاً موجوداً أقنوماً وكونه جوهراً أقنوماً لأنه ليس كل موجود جوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه لا تعلق له بغيره، وليس كل موجود باقياً، فيجب أن يكون كونه باقياً أقنوماً خامساً، ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك، وفيه ترك التثليث .
With two hypostases other than knowledge, it was said to them: Likewise, the knowledge of the Exalted Creator is His life, so it must be that He has two hypostases; and they have no answer for any of that. If one of them says: 'Hypostaticity is only established for the Creator by an attribute related to Himself, not connected to other than Him, and it is His being existent and substance referring to Himself, and His being living referring to Him and not connected to other than Him, and His being knowledgeable by Himself as an attribute referring by it to Himself; and He only has a hypostasis by His being knowledgeable by Himself, not by other than Him.' It is said to them: Likewise, He is eternal by Himself, and not every existing substance is eternal by itself? So it must be that His being eternal is a fourth hypostasis; and likewise His being everlasting is an attribute... It is a thing existing by itself and a substance by itself, so it must be that His being a thing existing is a hypostasis, and His being a substance is a hypostasis, because not every existing substance refers to itself, not connected to other than Him, and not every existing thing is everlasting, so it must be that His being everlasting is a fifth hypostasis, and they have no answer for that, and in it is the abandonment of the Trinity.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument against the Christian doctrine of three hypostases (aqānīm). The author presents a Christian claim that divine attributes like knowledge and life are hypostatic attributes pertaining only to God's essence, and then refutes it by showing that this logic leads to an infinite regress of hypostases. The Christian argues that only those attributes that refer solely to God's essence (e.g., being existent, substance, living, knowledgeable) constitute hypostases. The author responds: if that is the case, then His being eternal by Himself, His being everlasting, and even His being a thing and a substance would each have to be a distinct hypostasis, because not all things share these properties. Thus, the Christian would have to posit four or five hypostases, contradicting the doctrine of three. The argument ends by stating that this reasoning leads to abandoning the Trinity entirely.

Key Terms
أقنوم
الأقنومية
تثليث
باقنومين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Baqillani denies that God has attributes like knowledge and life.
Correction: Baqillani is not denying divine attributes; he is showing that the Christian definition of hypostasis leads to an absurd number of hypostases.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of Baqillani's argument against the Christian claim about hypostases?
A) To prove that God has exactly three hypostases.
B) To show that the Christian logic would require more than three hypostases.
C) To deny that God has attributes like knowledge and life.
D) To affirm that God is a substance.

Key Takeaway
Imam Baqillani demonstrates that the Christian definition of hypostasis leads to an indefinite number of hypostases, thereby refuting the Trinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you argue for your beliefs, do you apply the same logical criteria consistently to your own positions as you do to others? Or do you change the rules to protect what you want to believe? Take a moment to examine a recent disagreement—were you fair in your reasoning?
?
The Christians in this passage had a definition of 'hypostasis' that seemed neat, but Baqillani showed it was internally inconsistent. Are there areas of your faith where you hold to comfortable formulations without testing their internal coherence? Will you dare to examine them today?
?
Baqillani's argument forces the Christians to abandon their Trinity if they are consistent. Is there any cherished belief of yours that you would have to abandon if you were truly consistent? Are you willing to follow the truth wherever it leads, even if it means giving up something you hold dear?

The Common Substance Dilemma
A logical objection to the Trinity using the common substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic theologians exposed logical contradictions in the Christian doctrine of the Trinity by questioning the relationship between the 'common substance' and the three hypostases.

Core Idea
The 'common substance' dilemma shows that the Trinity is logically incoherent.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani presents a sharp logical objection to the Christian doctrine of the hypostases (aqānīm). He asks whether the 'common substance' that supposedly underlies the Father, Son, and Holy Spirit is identical to them or distinct. This seemingly simple question reveals a deep inconsistency: if the substance is the same as the hypostases, then they cannot be distinct; if it is different, then God is not one substance. Let's examine how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the text is cut off, but the core question is clear: the author asks about the relationship between the common substance and the hypostases.
The passage ends mid-sentence due to a footnote; the full argument is not present.
2
Identify the two possible answers
The author offers two possible replies: either the common substance is the hypostases or it is not. The Jacobites and Nestorians say it is not other than the hypostases.
This sets up a dilemma.
3
Consider the counter-question
The author then asks: 'Is not the substance undifferentiated...?' This implies that if the substance is the same, then the hypostases cannot have distinct properties.
The argument is incomplete, but the logical trap is evident.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: why does the author use this line of questioning? It is not to understand Christian doctrine but to show its inherent contradictions.
This is a classical kalam method of refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة عليهم في الأقانيم يقال لهم : خبروني عن الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم الذي هذه الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له
A question against them concerning the hypostases: It is said to them: Inform me about the common substance that encompasses the hypostases, which these hypostases have hypostases: Is it, in your view, the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: 'The substance is not other than the hypostases,' it is said: Is not the substance undifferentiated in terms of being a substance and in terms of not being numbered and in terms of not having?
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage introduces a new objection by the author against the Christian doctrine of hypostases. The author asks about the 'common substance' (al-jawhar al-ʿāmm) that encompasses the three hypostases: is this substance identical to the hypostases or distinct from them? He then presents the response of the Jacobites and Nestorians, who assert that the substance is not other than the hypostases. The author's counter-question begins: 'Is not the substance undifferentiated...' but the text breaks off. The implied argument is that if the substance is not distinct from the hypostases, then the hypostases cannot be distinct from each other, or the substance itself would be subject to differentiation, leading to contradictions. This question aims to expose inconsistency in the Christian position regarding the relationship between the one substance and the three hypostases.

Key Terms
جوهر عام
أقانيم
يعقوبية
نسطورية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the author is seeking clarification about Christian theology.
Correction: The author's aim is not to understand but to expose a logical flaw: the relationship between substance and hypostases is incoherent.

Checkpoint
What is the author's aim in asking about the common substance?
A) To determine which Christian sect is correct.
B) To show a logical contradiction in the relationship between the substance and hypostases.
C) To affirm that God is a substance without attributes.
D) To ask for a definition of substance.

Key Takeaway
The 'common substance' dilemma is a powerful argument that the Trinity is self-contradictory because it cannot coherently explain how one substance can be three distinct hypostases.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading this logical refutation of the Trinity, ask yourself: is your certainty in Tawhid merely intellectual agreement with an argument, or does it move your heart to humble submission? What concrete step can you take today to deepen your personal conviction in the oneness of Allah beyond rational proof?
?
If someone were to press you on why you believe in one God, would your answer rely entirely on arguments like this one, or does your faith stem from a lived relationship with Allah? How can you ensure that your knowledge translates into worship and trust?
?
This dilemma exposes a contradiction in the Trinity. Are there any contradictions in your own understanding or practice of Tawhid—such as loving worldly things more than Allah—that you have ignored? What will you do this week to align your heart fully with His oneness?

The Core Dilemma: Essence and Hypostases
Baqillani poses the dilemma and records the Jacobite/Nestorian answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial logical question that Baqillani poses to Trinitarian theologians, exposing the inherent tension in their beliefs.

Core Idea
If hypostases are the essence, they must be both differentiated and non‑differentiated — a contradiction.

Baqillani opens his refutation by asking a devastatingly simple question: Are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? The Jacobites and Nestorians answer that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani then points out that the essence is non‑differentiated, non‑counted, and without distinct properties, while the hypostases are differentiated, counted, and have distinct properties. This sets up the logical contradiction that will be developed later.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening question
Read the Arabic passage asking whether the hypostases are the essence or something else. Notice the direct and challenging tone.
Baqillani uses a rhetorical question to force an answer.
2
Identify the Jacobite/Nestorian response
They claim the essence is not other than the hypostases. Understand what this implies about identity.
3
Contrast the attributes of essence and hypostases
Baqillani then lists attributes: essence is non‑differentiated, non‑counted, without distinct properties; hypostases have opposite attributes. See the tension.
This contrast is the seed of the later contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟
اليعقوبية: وهم أصحاب يعقوب. قالوا بالأقانيم الثلاثة، إلا أنهم قالوا : انقلبت الكلمة لحماً ودماً، فصار الإله هو المسيح. وهو الظاهر بجسده، بل هو هو. وعنهم أخبرنا القرآن الكريم لقد كفر الذين قالوا إن الله هو المسيح ابن مريم فمنهم من قال: إن المسيح الله تعالى. ومنهم من قال ظهر اللاهوت بالناسوت فصار ناسوت المسيح مظهر الجوهرة، لا على طريق حلول جزء فيه، ولا على سبيل اتحاد الكلمة التي هي في حكم الصفة بل صار هو هو. وهذا كما يقال ظهر الملك بصورة إنسان، أو ظهر الشيطان بصورة حيوان وزعم قوم من اليعقوبية أن الكلمة لم تأخذ من مريم شيئاً، ولكنها مرت بها كالماء بالميزاب وما ظهر بها من شخص المسيح في الأعين فهو كالخيال والصورة في المرآة وإلا فما كان جسماً متجسماً كثيفاً في الحقيقة. وكذلك القتل والصلب وإنما وقع على الخيال والحسبان، وهؤلاء يقال لهم الإليانية وهم قوم بالشام واليمن وأرمينية قالوا : إنما صلب الإله أحلنا من حتى يخلصنا. وزعم بعضهم أن الكلمة كانت تدخل جسم المسيح عليه السلام أحياناً، فتصدر عنه الآيات من إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وتفارقه في بعض الأوقات فترد عليه الآلام والأوجاع.
النسطورية: أصحاب نسطور وقد تصرف في الأناجيل بحكم رأيه وإضافته إليهم إضافة المعتزلة إلى هذه الشريعة قال : إن الله تعالى واحد ذو أقانيم ثلاثة الوجود والعلم والحياة، وهذه الأقانيم ليست زائدة على الذات ولا هي هو واتحدت الكلمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام، لا على طريقة الامتزاج كما قالت الملكانية، ولا على طريقة الظهورية كما قالت اليعقوبية ولكن كإشراق الشمس في كوة على بلورة، وكظهور النقش في الشمع إذا طبع الخاتم وأشبه المذاهب بمذهب نسطور في الأقانيم : أحوال أبي هاشم من المعتزلة، فإنه يثبت خواص مختلفة لشيء واحد ويعني بقوله واحد يعني الإله . قال : هو واحد بالجوهر. أي ليس هو مركبا من جنسين بل هو بسيط وواحد. ويعني بالحياة والعلم اقنومين جوهرين، أي أصلين مبدأين للعالم. ثم فسر العلم بالنطق والكلمة . ويرجع منتهى كلامه إلى إثبات كونه تعالى موجوداً، حياً، ناطقاً كما تقول الفلاسفة في أحد الإنسان إلا أن هذه المعاني تتغاير في الإنسان ككونه جوهراً مركباً. وهو جوهر بسيط غير مركب. ومن النسطورية قوم يقال لهم المصلين قالوا في المسيح مثل ما قال نسطور إلا أنهم قالوا : إذا اجتهد الرجل في العبادة، وترك التغذي باللحم والدسم، ورفض الشهوات الحيوانية والنفسانية، تصفي جوهره حتى يبلغ ملكوت السموات ويرى الله تعالى جهرة وينكشف له ما في الغيب فلا تخفى عليه خافية الأرض ولا في السماء. ومن النسطورية من ينفي التشبيه، ويثبت القول بالقدر خيره وشره من العبد كما قالت القدرية.
ثم قيل لهم : أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الرُّوح ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدودٍ ولا مختلف ولا متحدٍ ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر ؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه.
فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم : إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذاً أربعة : جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا : الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة، قيل لهم : فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول : إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه.
The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: The essence is not other than the hypostases, it is said: Is not the essence non-different in that it is an essence, and in that it is not counted, and in that it does not have mutually distinct properties? The Jacobites: They are the followers of Jacob. They affirmed the three hypostases, except that they said: The Word turned into flesh and blood, so God became the Messiah. He is apparent with His body, rather He is He. And from them the noble Quran told us: 'Certainly disbelieved those who said that God is the Messiah, son of Mary.' Some of them said: The Messiah is God Almighty. Some of them said: The divinity appeared in the humanity, so the humanity of the Messiah became a manifestation of the essence, not by way of indwelling of a part in it, nor by way of union of the Word which is in the status of an attribute, but He became He. This is like saying the king appears in the form of a man, or the devil appears in the form of an animal. And a group of the Jacobites claimed that the Word did not take anything from Mary, but it passed through her like water through a spout, and what appeared of the person of the Messiah in the eyes is like an illusion and an image in a mirror; otherwise, it was not a thick, embodied body in reality. Likewise, the killing and crucifixion only occurred upon illusion and imagination. These are called the Elianites, and they are a people in Syria, Yemen, and Armenia. They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

Key Terms
الأقانيم
الجوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the Jacobites and Nestorians say about the relationship between the essence and the hypostases?
A) The essence is other than the hypostases.
B) The essence is not other than the hypostases.
C) The essence is only one of the hypostases.
D) The essence is unknowable.

Key Takeaway
The identity of essence and hypostases leads to a contradiction, because the essence is undifferentiated while the hypostases are differentiated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani forces his interlocutor to face a logical contradiction. When you hold a belief that feels comfortable, do you ever stop to examine whether it contains hidden inconsistencies? What belief in your own life might need such scrutiny?
?
The Jacobites and Nestorians replied honestly, yet their answer led to a dead end. In your own faith, are you more concerned with being right or with following truth wherever it leads, even if it means admitting a contradiction?
?
If you were standing before Baqillani and he asked you whether the hypostases are the essence or not, could you answer without contradicting yourself? What would your answer reveal about how deeply you think about your beliefs?

intermediate

Jacobite Christology: The Word Becomes Flesh
Baqillani details the Jacobite views on the incarnation and the nature of Christ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jacobite doctrine of the hypostases, including their view that the Word turned into flesh and that the divinity appeared in humanity.

Core Idea
The Jacobites believed the Word literally became flesh, so the Messiah is God himself manifested.

Having posed the initial question, Baqillani now describes the specific beliefs of the Jacobite sect. They hold that the Word transformed into flesh and blood, making the Messiah identical to God. He also recounts their various interpretations, including the idea that the Word passed through Mary like water through a spout, and that the crucifixion was only an illusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Jacobite belief summary
Read the passage describing the basic Jacobite position: the Word turned into flesh and the Messiah is God.
Notice the Quranic reference they claimed support from.
2
Identify the two sub‑interpretations
The passage presents two subgroups: one says divinity appeared in humanity (manifestation), another says the Word passed through Mary without taking anything.
The second group is called the Elianites.
3
Note the view on crucifixion
Some Jacobites claimed the crucifixion was only an illusion, and some said the Word entered and left the body of Christ.
This shows the variety within the sect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟
اليعقوبية: وهم أصحاب يعقوب. قالوا بالأقانيم الثلاثة، إلا أنهم قالوا : انقلبت الكلمة لحماً ودماً، فصار الإله هو المسيح. وهو الظاهر بجسده، بل هو هو. وعنهم أخبرنا القرآن الكريم لقد كفر الذين قالوا إن الله هو المسيح ابن مريم فمنهم من قال: إن المسيح الله تعالى. ومنهم من قال ظهر اللاهوت بالناسوت فصار ناسوت المسيح مظهر الجوهرة، لا على طريق حلول جزء فيه، ولا على سبيل اتحاد الكلمة التي هي في حكم الصفة بل صار هو هو. وهذا كما يقال ظهر الملك بصورة إنسان، أو ظهر الشيطان بصورة حيوان وزعم قوم من اليعقوبية أن الكلمة لم تأخذ من مريم شيئاً، ولكنها مرت بها كالماء بالميزاب وما ظهر بها من شخص المسيح في الأعين فهو كالخيال والصورة في المرآة وإلا فما كان جسماً متجسماً كثيفاً في الحقيقة. وكذلك القتل والصلب وإنما وقع على الخيال والحسبان، وهؤلاء يقال لهم الإليانية وهم قوم بالشام واليمن وأرمينية قالوا : إنما صلب الإله أحلنا من حتى يخلصنا. وزعم بعضهم أن الكلمة كانت تدخل جسم المسيح عليه السلام أحياناً، فتصدر عنه الآيات من إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وتفارقه في بعض الأوقات فترد عليه الآلام والأوجاع.
النسطورية: أصحاب نسطور وقد تصرف في الأناجيل بحكم رأيه وإضافته إليهم إضافة المعتزلة إلى هذه الشريعة قال : إن الله تعالى واحد ذو أقانيم ثلاثة الوجود والعلم والحياة، وهذه الأقانيم ليست زائدة على الذات ولا هي هو واتحدت الكلمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام، لا على طريقة الامتزاج كما قالت الملكانية، ولا على طريقة الظهورية كما قالت اليعقوبية ولكن كإشراق الشمس في كوة على بلورة، وكظهور النقش في الشمع إذا طبع الخاتم وأشبه المذاهب بمذهب نسطور في الأقانيم : أحوال أبي هاشم من المعتزلة، فإنه يثبت خواص مختلفة لشيء واحد ويعني بقوله واحد يعني الإله . قال : هو واحد بالجوهر. أي ليس هو مركبا من جنسين بل هو بسيط وواحد. ويعني بالحياة والعلم اقنومين جوهرين، أي أصلين مبدأين للعالم. ثم فسر العلم بالنطق والكلمة . ويرجع منتهى كلامه إلى إثبات كونه تعالى موجوداً، حياً، ناطقاً كما تقول الفلاسفة في أحد الإنسان إلا أن هذه المعاني تتغاير في الإنسان ككونه جوهراً مركباً. وهو جوهر بسيط غير مركب. ومن النسطورية قوم يقال لهم المصلين قالوا في المسيح مثل ما قال نسطور إلا أنهم قالوا : إذا اجتهد الرجل في العبادة، وترك التغذي باللحم والدسم، ورفض الشهوات الحيوانية والنفسانية، تصفي جوهره حتى يبلغ ملكوت السموات ويرى الله تعالى جهرة وينكشف له ما في الغيب فلا تخفى عليه خافية الأرض ولا في السماء. ومن النسطورية من ينفي التشبيه، ويثبت القول بالقدر خيره وشره من العبد كما قالت القدرية.
ثم قيل لهم : أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الرُّوح ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدودٍ ولا مختلف ولا متحدٍ ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر ؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه.
فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم : إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذاً أربعة : جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا : الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة، قيل لهم : فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول : إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه.
The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: The essence is not other than the hypostases, it is said: Is not the essence non-different in that it is an essence, and in that it is not counted, and in that it does not have mutually distinct properties? The Jacobites: They are the followers of Jacob. They affirmed the three hypostases, except that they said: The Word turned into flesh and blood, so God became the Messiah. He is apparent with His body, rather He is He. And from them the noble Quran told us: 'Certainly disbelieved those who said that God is the Messiah, son of Mary.' Some of them said: The Messiah is God Almighty. Some of them said: The divinity appeared in the humanity, so the humanity of the Messiah became a manifestation of the essence, not by way of indwelling of a part in it, nor by way of union of the Word which is in the status of an attribute, but He became He. This is like saying the king appears in the form of a man, or the devil appears in the form of an animal. And a group of the Jacobites claimed that the Word did not take anything from Mary, but it passed through her like water through a spout, and what appeared of the person of the Messiah in the eyes is like an illusion and an image in a mirror; otherwise, it was not a thick, embodied body in reality. Likewise, the killing and crucifixion only occurred upon illusion and imagination. These are called the Elianites, and they are a people in Syria, Yemen, and Armenia. They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all Jacobites held a single, unified doctrine on the incarnation.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Jacobites were divided into at least three distinct subgroups, each with different explanations of how the Word related to Christ's body.

Checkpoint
What did the Elianite subgroup of Jacobites believe about the crucifixion?
A) It was a real, physical event.
B) It was an illusion and only appeared to happen.
C) It was only a spiritual crucifixion.
D) It did not happen at all.

Key Takeaway
The Jacobites had several conflicting interpretations of how the Word became flesh, revealing the instability of their doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran's warning against those who say 'God is the Messiah,' do you ever catch yourself thinking of Jesus in ways that blur the line between human and Divine—how would you defend Islamic monotheism if challenged by a Christian?
?
The Jacobite belief that the Word passed through Mary like water through a spout reduces the Messiah to a mere apparition. Are there ways you might be treating your own faith or actions as mere appearances—going through the motions without real substance?
?
The Elianites claimed the crucifixion was an illusion to avoid the shame of the cross. Is there a painful reality in your life that you are tempted to treat as unreal to avoid confronting it?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
8 min
Nestorian Doctrine: Union Without Mixing
Baqillani details the Nestorian views on the hypostases and the union of the Word with Christ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Nestorian view of the Trinity and the union of the Word with Christ, as well as its resemblance to the Mu'tazilite theory of states (ahwal).

Core Idea
Nestorius taught a union of the Word with Christ like sunlight on a crystal, not by mixture or manifestation.

Baqillani then turns to the Nestorians, followers of Nestorius. They affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and describe the union of the Word with Jesus as an intimate connection without mixing or manifestation. Baqillani notes the similarity to Abu Hashim's theory of states, and also mentions other Nestorian subgroups.

Guided Path
1
Read the Nestorian belief summary
Read the passage about Nestorius's doctrine: three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and the union of the Word with Christ.
Notice the analogy of sunlight shining through a skylight onto a crystal.
2
Compare with Mu'tazilite states
Baqillani points out the similarity to Abu Hashim's theory of states (ahwal). Understand why he makes this comparison.
This shows the philosophical influences on Nestorianism.
3
Identify the sub‑sects
The passage mentions a group called 'the Prayers' and another that negates anthropomorphism and affirms predestination.
These show further fragmentation.

الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟

The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Nestorius's union of the Word with Christ is identical to the Jacobite or Melkite views.
Correction: Baqillani clearly distinguishes Nestorian union as neither mixing (Melkite) nor manifestation (Jacobite), but as a third type akin to sunlight on crystal.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, which Mu'tazilite thinker's theory resembles Nestorius's view on the hypostases?
A) Wasil ibn Ata
B) Abu Hashim
C) Al-Ashari
D) Al-Maturidi

Key Takeaway
Nestorius advocated a union of the Word with Christ that is neither mixing nor manifestation, resembling the Mu'tazilite theory of states.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Nestorians claimed to uphold God's oneness yet introduced distinctions that ultimately compromised it. In your own life, do you ever try to reconcile contradictory beliefs about Allah by using intellectual gymnastics, all while claiming to follow revelation? Where might you be prioritizing your reasoning over a clear text?
?
The 'Prayers' subgroup believed extreme asceticism could purify the soul to see Allah directly. Are there any religious practices you perform that you secretly think earn you special access to Allah, forgetting that even the Prophet ﷺ was told to strive but hope for mercy? Is your worship driven by expectation of reward or by love and submission?
?
Nestorius manipulated the Gospels to fit his opinion. When you read the Quran, do you ever find yourself interpreting verses in a way that softens a command you find difficult? Be specific: what is one verse you have rationalized away rather than obeyed?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate

The Logical Refutation of Trinitarian Claims
Baqillani refutes the Jacobite/Nestorian and Melkite positions using logical contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical arguments that expose contradictions in both the Jacobite/Nestorian and the Melkite positions.

Core Idea
If the essence is the hypostases, it must be both undifferentiated and differentiated; if the essence is other than the hypostases, there are four gods or a redundant fourth.

After detailing the various Trinitarian beliefs, Baqillani delivers the crushing logical blow. He first refutes the Jacobite/Nestorian position by showing that if the essence is the hypostases, then the essence would have contradictory attributes. He then refutes the Melkite position by arguing that if the essence is distinct from the hypostases, either there are four gods or the essence is redundant. Both alternatives are absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of Jacobites/Nestorians
Read the argument: if the essence is the hypostases and the hypostases are differentiated, counted, and one unites with humanity, then the essence must be both undifferentiated and differentiated — a contradiction.
Notice the use of the question 'Afalaysa...' to elicit agreement.
2
Read the refutation of Melkites
If the essence is other than the hypostases, then the three hypostases plus the essence make four gods. If they claim only the hypostases are gods, then the essence is redundant.
Baqillani shows that the Melkite position collapses into polytheism or nonsense.
3
Reflect on the method
Baqillani uses pure logic without relying on scripture. He forces the opponent into impossible positions.
This is a classic kalam argumentative technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟
اليعقوبية: وهم أصحاب يعقوب. قالوا بالأقانيم الثلاثة، إلا أنهم قالوا : انقلبت الكلمة لحماً ودماً، فصار الإله هو المسيح. وهو الظاهر بجسده، بل هو هو. وعنهم أخبرنا القرآن الكريم لقد كفر الذين قالوا إن الله هو المسيح ابن مريم فمنهم من قال: إن المسيح الله تعالى. ومنهم من قال ظهر اللاهوت بالناسوت فصار ناسوت المسيح مظهر الجوهرة، لا على طريق حلول جزء فيه، ولا على سبيل اتحاد الكلمة التي هي في حكم الصفة بل صار هو هو. وهذا كما يقال ظهر الملك بصورة إنسان، أو ظهر الشيطان بصورة حيوان وزعم قوم من اليعقوبية أن الكلمة لم تأخذ من مريم شيئاً، ولكنها مرت بها كالماء بالميزاب وما ظهر بها من شخص المسيح في الأعين فهو كالخيال والصورة في المرآة وإلا فما كان جسماً متجسماً كثيفاً في الحقيقة. وكذلك القتل والصلب وإنما وقع على الخيال والحسبان، وهؤلاء يقال لهم الإليانية وهم قوم بالشام واليمن وأرمينية قالوا : إنما صلب الإله أحلنا من حتى يخلصنا. وزعم بعضهم أن الكلمة كانت تدخل جسم المسيح عليه السلام أحياناً، فتصدر عنه الآيات من إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وتفارقه في بعض الأوقات فترد عليه الآلام والأوجاع.
النسطورية: أصحاب نسطور وقد تصرف في الأناجيل بحكم رأيه وإضافته إليهم إضافة المعتزلة إلى هذه الشريعة قال : إن الله تعالى واحد ذو أقانيم ثلاثة الوجود والعلم والحياة، وهذه الأقانيم ليست زائدة على الذات ولا هي هو واتحدت الكلمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام، لا على طريقة الامتزاج كما قالت الملكانية، ولا على طريقة الظهورية كما قالت اليعقوبية ولكن كإشراق الشمس في كوة على بلورة، وكظهور النقش في الشمع إذا طبع الخاتم وأشبه المذاهب بمذهب نسطور في الأقانيم : أحوال أبي هاشم من المعتزلة، فإنه يثبت خواص مختلفة لشيء واحد ويعني بقوله واحد يعني الإله . قال : هو واحد بالجوهر. أي ليس هو مركبا من جنسين بل هو بسيط وواحد. ويعني بالحياة والعلم اقنومين جوهرين، أي أصلين مبدأين للعالم. ثم فسر العلم بالنطق والكلمة . ويرجع منتهى كلامه إلى إثبات كونه تعالى موجوداً، حياً، ناطقاً كما تقول الفلاسفة في أحد الإنسان إلا أن هذه المعاني تتغاير في الإنسان ككونه جوهراً مركباً. وهو جوهر بسيط غير مركب. ومن النسطورية قوم يقال لهم المصلين قالوا في المسيح مثل ما قال نسطور إلا أنهم قالوا : إذا اجتهد الرجل في العبادة، وترك التغذي باللحم والدسم، ورفض الشهوات الحيوانية والنفسانية، تصفي جوهره حتى يبلغ ملكوت السموات ويرى الله تعالى جهرة وينكشف له ما في الغيب فلا تخفى عليه خافية الأرض ولا في السماء. ومن النسطورية من ينفي التشبيه، ويثبت القول بالقدر خيره وشره من العبد كما قالت القدرية.
ثم قيل لهم : أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الرُّوح ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدودٍ ولا مختلف ولا متحدٍ ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر ؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه.
فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم : إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذاً أربعة : جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا : الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة، قيل لهم : فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول : إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه.
The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: The essence is not other than the hypostases, it is said: Is not the essence non-different in that it is an essence, and in that it is not counted, and in that it does not have mutually distinct properties? The Jacobites: They are the followers of Jacob. They affirmed the three hypostases, except that they said: The Word turned into flesh and blood, so God became the Messiah. He is apparent with His body, rather He is He. And from them the noble Quran told us: 'Certainly disbelieved those who said that God is the Messiah, son of Mary.' Some of them said: The Messiah is God Almighty. Some of them said: The divinity appeared in the humanity, so the humanity of the Messiah became a manifestation of the essence, not by way of indwelling of a part in it, nor by way of union of the Word which is in the status of an attribute, but He became He. This is like saying the king appears in the form of a man, or the devil appears in the form of an animal. And a group of the Jacobites claimed that the Word did not take anything from Mary, but it passed through her like water through a spout, and what appeared of the person of the Messiah in the eyes is like an illusion and an image in a mirror; otherwise, it was not a thick, embodied body in reality. Likewise, the killing and crucifixion only occurred upon illusion and imagination. These are called the Elianites, and they are a people in Syria, Yemen, and Armenia. They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Trinitarian doctrines are beyond rational critique and can only be accepted by faith.
Correction: Baqillani shows that Trinitarian claims lead to straightforward logical contradictions, making them untenable even without appealing to revelation.

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence if the Melkites claim that the essence is other than the hypostases?
A) There are exactly three gods.
B) There are four gods or the essence is redundant.
C) The hypostases become the essence.
D) The Trinity remains intact.

Key Takeaway
Trinitarian doctrines, whether claiming identity or distinction between essence and hypostases, lead to logical absurdities: either contradiction or polytheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson exposes logical contradictions in a widely held doctrine. Have you ever accepted a belief—religious or otherwise—on authority alone without testing its internal consistency? Will you commit to examining your own convictions with the same rigorous logic Baqillani applied here?
?
Baqillani's arguments require no scripture, only reason. Do you trust that your intellect is sufficient to discern truth in matters of faith? Or do you fear that rational scrutiny might undermine your beliefs? Pledge to use your mind fearlessly for the sake of truth.
?
The Melkite position reduces their fourth essence to a meaningless redundancy. Are there practices or beliefs in your life that you maintain but which are functionally redundant? What would it cost you to strip them away? Ask Allah for the courage to abandon what is superfluous and embrace pure tawheed.
