Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
Refutation of Essence-Hypostases Identity
Baqillani refutes the identity of essence and hypostases via contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why identifying the divine essence with the hypostases leads to an untenable contradiction regarding divine simplicity.

Core Idea
If the essence is the hypostases, it becomes multiple and changing — contradicting divine oneness.

Baqillani begins by engaging the Christian claim that the divine essence (al-jawhar) is identical with the three hypostases. Through a simple yet devastating line of questioning, he exposes the logical outcome of this identification: if the hypostases are distinct, counted, and one of them united with Christ's body, then the essence itself must share these properties, contradicting its supposed unity and immutability.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Christian claim
Read the opening question: do the hypostases have distinct meanings? The Christian affirms. Note that this sets up the trap.
The opponent agrees the hypostases are distinct properties.
2
Follow the logical consequences
If the essence is the hypostases, then the essence inherits all their attributes: being multiple, counted, and even uniting with Christ. Trace how Baqillani draws this conclusion.
3
Recognize the contradiction
The essence is supposed to be one, uncounted, and unchanging. The conclusion that it is multiple and united with Christ creates an absurdity. This shows the identity claim is false.
The contradiction is between divine simplicity and the multiplicity of the hypostases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خواص متباينة المعنى؟ فإن قالوا: أجل، وهو قولهم، قيل لهم: أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الروح؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم: فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد، وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدود ولا مختلف ولا متحد ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه. فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم: إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم: فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذا أربعة: جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا: الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة قيل لهم: فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول: إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه. ويقال لهم: إن جاز أن يكون الرابع مع الثلاثة ثلاثة فقط، فما أنكرتم أن يكون الروح والعلم مع الإله الموجود واحداً فقط وأن يكون أقنوماً واحداً ولا يكون الثاني والثالث شيئاً يزيد على الواحد كما لم يكن الرابع شيئاً يزيد على الثالث فتكون الثلاثة الأقانيم هي جوهر واحد كما كانت الأربعة التي منها الجوهر ثلاثة؛ ولا جواب عن ذلك.
Properties with distinct meanings? If they say: Yes, that is their statement, it is said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are properties with distinct meanings, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son from them put on and united with the body of the Messiah peace be upon him without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, necessarily, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specification, and among them is the one that united, and they are the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not distinct in meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct in meaning, united one; this is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence; and there is no escape from it. If the Melkites among them, the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it; and this invalidates your statement of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between the statement that there are three hypostases and no essence that gathers them and belongs to them, and the statement that there are three hypostases and a comprehensive essence for them; so it must be that the existence of the fourth is like its non-existence and its affirmation like its negation; this is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it. And it is said to them: If it is permissible that the fourth with the three is only three, then why do you deny that the Spirit and Knowledge with the existing God are only one and that it is one hypostasis, and the second and third are not something additional to the one, just as the fourth was not something additional to the third, so that the three hypostases are one essence just as the four, including the essence, were three; and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian claim that the divine essence (جوهر) is identical with the three hypostases (أقانيم). The argument proceeds stepwise:
1. The author begins by asking whether the hypostases are distinct properties. The opponent agrees that they have distinct meanings, are counted, and that the Son uniquely united with Christ's body. From this, Baqillani draws the consequence: if the essence is the hypostases, then the essence itself must share these properties—it becomes multiple, distinct, and subject to union with Christ. But the essence is supposed to be one, uncounted, and unchanging. Thus the identification leads to a contradiction.
2. Then the author considers the Melkite position that the essence is distinct from the hypostases. If the essence is God and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there are four gods, contradicting trinity.
3. If they avoid this by saying the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then the essence is superfluous, and its existence or non-existence makes no difference—another absurdity.
4. Finally, Baqillani argues that if the fourth can be counted as three when combined with the three hypostases, then by analogy the Spirit and Knowledge could be one hypostasis, reducing the Trinity to a single hypostasis, which undermines their doctrine. The passage concludes that there is no answer to this refutation.

Key Terms
جوهر
أقانيم
متباينة
معدودة
ناسوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hypostases are merely modes or properties of the divine essence, so identity does not imply multiplicity.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the hypostases are considered distinct and counted, so if they are the essence, the essence becomes multiple—contradicting divine simplicity.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani conclude if the essence is identical with the hypostases?
A) The essence remains one and simple.
B) The essence becomes multiple and united with Christ.
C) The hypostases become one.
D) The Trinity is preserved.

Key Takeaway
Identifying the divine essence with the hypostases forces the essence to become multiple and mutable, which is impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about God that, upon reflection, led to a contradiction with His oneness? What did you do to resolve it? Now, examine your current understanding: Are there any subtle compromises on tawhid you need to correct today?
?
The passage shows that even well-intentioned descriptions of God can inadvertently produce contradictions. When you speak about God's attributes, do you allow Him to be as He described Himself, or do you impose human categories? Will you commit to studying the Qur'an and Sunnah with a scholar to purify your understanding?
?
Baqillani's argument forces the opponent to face the logical consequences of their claim. Are you willing to subject your own theological positions to the same rigorous scrutiny? What is one belief you hold that you have not critically examined? Set a time to investigate it thoroughly with a reliable source.

Refutation of Essence-Hypostases Distinction
Baqillani refutes the distinction of essence and hypostases via dilemmas and counting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why distinguishing the essence from the hypostases leads to either four gods or a superfluous fourth, and why the counting argument undermines the Trinity.

Core Idea
If essence is distinct from hypostases, either four gods or a useless fourth entity results.

Baqillani now turns to the Melkite (Roman Christian) position that the divine essence is distinct from the hypostases. He presents a dilemma: if the essence is God and the hypostases are gods, then there are four gods; if the essence is not god, then it is redundant. Finally, he uses a clever counting argument to show that the Trinity could be reduced to a single hypostasis, exposing the inconsistency of their doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Examine the Melkite distinction
Read the dilemma: if essence is distinct and both are gods, there are four gods; if essence is not god, it is unnecessary.
The Melkites claim essence ≠ hypostases.
2
Analyze the counting argument
The fourth (essence) with the three hypostases is still considered three? Follow the logic: if the fourth adds nothing, then by analogy, the Spirit and Knowledge could be one hypostasis, reducing the Trinity to one.
This shows the arbitrariness of their enumeration.
3
Appreciate the final conclusion
The argument leaves the Christian with no answer, exposing the incoherence of the Trinity doctrine.

Baqillani's Refutation of Tritheism
Baqillani refutes the Nestorian and Jacobite statement that each hypostasis is God yet they are one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Christian Trinity as described by the Nestorians and Jacobites is logically self-contradictory according to Baqillani.

Core Idea
Three gods cannot be one God without contradiction.

In this brief but decisive passage, Imam Baqillani takes aim at the Christian doctrine of the Trinity as formulated by the Nestorians and Jacobites. He points out the immediate logical problem: if each hypostasis (Father, Son, Spirit) is fully God, then there are three gods. The claim that they are one God is then meaningless. This lesson will unpack that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English side by side to grasp the concise argument.
2
Identify the claim being refuted
Note the exact statement: Father is God, Son is God, Spirit is God, yet they are one. This is the target.
3
Understand the logical contradiction
Baqillani reasons that if each is God, then there are three gods. Calling them one contradicts the assignment of divinity to each.
4
Ask why this refutation matters
Consider how Baqillani uses simple logic (non-contradiction) to challenge a foundational Christian belief.
This shows the kalam approach of holding claims to rational consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يقال لهم وللنسطورية واليعقوبية في قولهم: «إن الأب إله وإن الابن إله وإن الروح إله وإن الآلهة مع ذلك واحد»؛ لأنه إذا كان كل واحد منهم ثلاثة آلهة؛ ولا معنى لقولهم إله واحد، وهم قد جعلوا الإلهية لكل واحد منهم.
And likewise it is said to them and to the Nestorians and Jacobites regarding their statement: 'Indeed the Father is God, and the Son is God, and the Spirit is God, and the gods with that are one'; because if each one of them is three gods, there is no meaning to their statement 'one God', while they have assigned divinity to every single one of them.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a brief refutation of the Nestorian and Jacobite doctrine that each of the three hypostases—Father, Son, and Holy Spirit—is God, yet they are one God. Baqillani points out the logical contradiction: if each hypostasis is individually God, then there are three gods. To then claim that these three gods are one God is meaningless because 'one God' cannot consist of three distinct divine individuals. The assignment of divinity to each hypostasis results in tritheism, not monotheism.

Key Terms

ابن
روح القدس
إله

تثليث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may assume the Christian Trinity is a mystery beyond logic that cannot be rationally assessed.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Trinity as described (each hypostasis fully God yet one God) is a straightforward logical contradiction that violates the principle of non-contradiction.

B) It denies the divinity of the Son.
C) It implies the essence is divisible.
D) It confuses the hypostases with properties.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that claiming each hypostasis is God leads logically to tritheism, not monotheism.

?

Can you name one inherited assumption about God that you have not critically examined? What step will you take to verify it?
?

Consider your own worship: Are there any acts you perform that you call 'for Allah alone' but in your heart you seek recognition from others or rely on your own strength? Will you repent and realign your intention before your next prayer?

Baqillani's Dilemma: Essence and Hypostases
Baqillani poses a dilemma to the Melkites about essence and hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a strategic question to force a logical dilemma on the Melkite Trinity doctrine.

Core Idea
A well-crafted question can expose internal contradictions in a rival theology.

Baqillani poses a concise but devastating dilemma to the Melkites. By asking whether the divine essence is similar or different from the three hypostases, he sets up a logical trap. No matter which answer they give, it leads to an inconsistency with their own premises. This lesson examines the structure of this kind of argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure of the question and the two options presented.
The passage is incomplete; the response is cut off.
2
Identify the two options
Baqillani offers two possibilities: the essence is either similar (موافق) or different (مخالف) from the hypostases. Understand what each option implies.
3
Consider the logical consequences
Think about what follows if they say 'similar' — the essence would share attributes with the hypostases, implying multiplicity in the essence. If 'different' — the essence is disconnected from the hypostases, contradicting their unity.
4
Speculate on the missing part
The text cuts off after 'قيل لهم' (it is said to them). Imagine what Baqillani would argue next based on the dilemma. How would he refute each answer?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى على الملكية يقال لهم: خبرونا عن الجوهر الذي هو عندكم غير الأقانيم: أهو ذلك مخالف لها أو موافق لها؟ فإن قالوا: إنه موافق لها قيل لهم:
Another question against the Melkites. It is said to them: Inform us about the essence which with you is other than the hypostases: is it that which is different from them or similar to them? If they say: It is similar to them, it is said to them:
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents a new question directed at the Melkites, who hold that the divine essence (جوهر) is distinct from the three hypostases (أقانيم). Baqillani asks: Is this essence similar (موافق) or different (مخالف) from the hypostases? The question is designed to force a dilemma. If they say it is similar, then the essence shares attributes with the hypostases, leading to plurality in the essence—contradicting its simplicity. If they say it is different, then the essence would be unlike the hypostases, raising questions about how it relates to them. Unfortunately, the page ends before presenting the full argument; the text cuts off at 'قيل لهم:' (it is said to them), so the intended refutation is not fully given in this window.

أقانيم
مخالف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The question is a simple factual inquiry about similarity.
Correction: It is a logical trap: either answer leads to a contradiction with Melkite premises.

Checkpoint

A) Whether the essence is created or uncreated.
B) Whether the essence is similar or different from the hypostases.
C) Whether the hypostases are eternal.
D) Whether the essence is one or three.

Key Takeaway
A single well-posed question can force a rival theology into a logical contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If your own theology were subjected to this kind of 'similar or different' dilemma, which horn would you be stuck on? And are you ready to honestly answer that question before God?

Refuting the Trinity: The Incoherence of Distinct Hypostases
Baqillani refutes the Trinity argument from hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the Christian Trinity doctrine, specifically how the claim that the hypostases add nothing to the divine essence undermines their distinctness.

Core Idea
If hypostases add nothing, why stop at three?

The Christian doctrine of the Trinity asserts that God exists as three distinct hypostases (Father, Son, Holy Spirit) sharing one essence. Baqillani challenges this by exposing a logical flaw: if the second and third hypostases add nothing to the first, then by the same logic a fourth would add nothing, and so on. This reveals the arbitrariness of the claim and refutes the notion of distinct hypostases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
Read the passage and notice the claim that the Spirit and Knowledge are one with God as one hypostasis, and that the second and third add nothing to the first.
This is the Trinitarian position Baqillani is targeting.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Baqillani extends the logic: if the second and third add nothing, then a fourth would also add nothing. This leads to an absurd multiplication of hypostases.
The argument shows the criterion of 'adding nothing' does not limit hypostases to three.
3
Understand the conclusion
If three hypostases can be one essence because they add nothing, then four or more can also be one essence. The opponent's distinction collapses.
Baqillani asserts there is no answer to this refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنكرتم أن يكون الرُّوح والعلم مع الإله الموجود واحداً فقط وأن يكون أقنوماً واحداً ولا يكون الثاني والثالث شيئاً يزيد على الواحد كما لم يكن الرابع شيئاً يزيد على الثالث فتكون الثلاثة الأقانيم هي جوهر واحد كما كانت الأربعة التي منها الجوهر ثلاثة ؛ ولا جواب عن ذلك.
You denied that the Spirit and the Knowledge are with the existing God one only, and that they are one hypostasis, and that the second and third are nothing that adds to the one, just as the fourth is nothing that adds to the third, so the three hypostases are one essence, just as the four, from which the essence is three; and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the Trinity. Baqillani argues against the claim that the Spirit and the Word (Knowledge) are one with God but are distinct hypostases. He uses a reductio ad absurdum: if the second and third hypostases add nothing to the first, then by the same logic a fourth would add nothing to the third, so you could have four hypostases and still call them one essence. This shows the incoherence of the Trinitarian claim that three distinct hypostases are one essence without any addition.

Key Terms
الرُّوح
العلم
الإله الموجود
أقنوم
جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Trinity is logically consistent because the three hypostases are distinct but one essence without addition.
Correction: Baqillani shows that if distinct hypostases add nothing to the essence, then any number of hypostases could be added, making the distinction arbitrary and incoherent.

Checkpoint
What logical consequence does Baqillani derive from the claim that the second and third hypostases add nothing to the first?
A) The second and third are equal to the first.
B) A fourth hypostasis would also add nothing, making the four one essence.
C) The essence is divisible into three parts.
D) The hypostases are not eternal.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Trinity by exposing that if distinct hypostases add nothing to the essence, there is no logical limit to their number, rendering the doctrine incoherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you encounter a challenge to your faith, do you search for a coherent rational defense, or do you retreat into comfortable dogmas? Baqillani forces an opponent into a corner—are you ready to be similarly challenged?
?
This argument exposes the incoherence of claiming distinct yet non-additive hypostases. Is there any area of your own belief where you accept contradictory propositions because they feel right? Will you examine them honestly today?

Refutation of Three Gods Claiming Oneness
Baqillani refutes the Trinity's claim of oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical argument against the Trinity's claim to be one God while each person is fully God.

Core Idea
If each person is fully God, they cannot be numerically one.

Baqillani addresses the Christian claim that Father, Son, and Spirit are each God yet still one God. He exposes a logical contradiction: if each is God, then there are three gods, not one. This passage is a classic refutation of Trinitarian theology from a monotheistic perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the structure of the claim: 'The Father is God, the Son is God, the Spirit is God, and the God is with that one.' Note how Baqillani responds.
2
Identify the logical contradiction
Baqillani argues that if each person is God, then there are three gods. The phrase 'three gods' emphasizes the contradiction. Ask: Why does saying each is God make them three?
Consider the principle: if A=God and B=God and A≠B, then there are at least two gods unless they are identical in every way, which the Trinity denies.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'one God'
Baqillani concludes that their statement 'one God' has no meaning because they have assigned divinity to each person. Reflect on how this argument targets the coherence of the Trinity.
This shows the Islamic critique that Trinitarian doctrine is logically inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يقال لهم وللنسطورية واليعقوبية في قولهم: «إن الأب إله وإن الابن إله وإن الروح إله وإن الإله مع ذلك واحد» ؛ لأنه إذا كان كل واحد منهم ثلاثة آلهة ؛ ولا معنى لقولهم إله واحد ، وهم قد جعلوا الإلهية لكل واحد منهم.
And likewise it is said to them, and to the Nestorians and Jacobites, regarding their statement: 'The Father is God, and the Son is God, and the Spirit is God, and the God is with that one'; because if each one of them is three gods, there is no meaning to their statement 'one God', and they have made divinity for each one of them.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the common Christian statement that the Father, Son, and Holy Spirit are each God yet they are one God. Baqillani points out the contradiction: if each person is God, then there are three gods, not one. The phrase 'three gods' here is likely a rhetorical simplification—he means that attributing full divinity to each results in three distinct gods. He then notes that they have assigned divinity to each, undermining any claim to monotheism.

A) Because they deny the divinity of the Son.
B) Because they have made each one a separate god, so they have three gods.
C) Because they worship only one person.
D) Because they believe in a hierarchy among the persons.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani exposes that affirming full divinity for each person necessarily entails three gods, making the claim of oneness meaningless.

?

Refutation of the Melkite Essence-Hypostases Distinction
Baqillani refutes the Melkite distinction between essence and hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a dialectical dilemma to refute the Melkite claim that the divine essence is distinct from the three hypostases.

Core Idea
The Melkite distinction between essence and hypostases leads to logical contradictions.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani engages in a polemical debate with the Melkite Christians. He presents a dilemma that forces them into absurd consequences, demonstrating that their doctrine cannot be rationally maintained. Follow the logical steps as he systematically dismantles their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the dialectical format: Baqillani poses a question, gives the opponent's hypothetical answer, and then refutes it.
2
Identify the two alternatives
The passage presents two alternatives: (1) the essence agrees wholly with the hypostases, or (2) it agrees only in essentiality but differs in hypostaticity. Find these two parts in the text.
3
Analyze the first alternative
If the essence agrees wholly, then it must itself be a son, spirit, and a property for another fifth essence. Notice the absurd consequences that follow.
Baqillani uses reductio ad absurdum: if agreement implies identity, the essence becomes multiple and contradictory.
4
Analyze the second alternative
If the essence agrees only in essentiality but differs in hypostaticity, then the same attribute (essentiality) becomes both the point of agreement and difference. See how Baqillani forces a contradiction.
The opponent tries to separate respects, but Baqillani shows that the difference must be either essence or accident, which cannot be.
5
Reflect on the overall lesson
Consider why this refutation is important: it shows that Trinitarian distinctions cannot be rationally defended without falling into inconsistency.
This is a classic example of Islamic theological polemics against Christian doctrines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى على الملكية يقال لهم : خبرونا عن الجوهر الذي هو عندكم غير الأقانيم : أهو ذلك مخالف لها أو موافق لها؟ فإن قالوا : إنه موافق لها قيل لهم : فيجب أن يكون أقانيم مثلها، وأن يكون الجوهر ابناً من حيث وافق الابن، وأن يكون روحاً من حيث وافق الروح، وأن يكون أقنوماً، وخاصاً لجوهر آخر خامس كما أن الأقانيم خواص لجوهر ويجب أيضاً أن تكون نفسه متباينة من حيث أشبهت أقانيم مختلفة المعاني وأن يكون ابن نفسه نفسه لأنه مثل ابنه وروحه وبمعناهما؛ وهذا جهل عظيم وترك لقولهم إن المعنى مختلف صاروا إليه. وإن قالوا : ليس الجوهر موافقاً للأقانيم من كل جهة، وإنما يوافقها بالجوهرية لأن جوهرها من جوهره وإنما يخالفها في القنومية، قيل لهم : فالجهة التي وافقها بها وهي الجوهرية هي الجهة التي خالفها بها وهي القنومية؛ فإن قالوا نعم جعلوا معنى الجوهرية هو معنى القنومية، وقيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون الجوهر أقنوماً لجوهر آخر ولنفسه؟ وذلك ترك قولهم. فإن قالوا : جهة الاختلاف بينهما وهي القنومية غير جهة الاتفاق التي هي الجوهرية قيل لهم : فيجب أن يكون هناك خلاف ثابت بين الجوهر والأقانيم في القنومية، وأن يكون ذلك الخلاف لا يعدو أن يكون جوهراً أو عرضاً، وإلا وجب أن يوافقها بنفسه في الجوهرية ويخالفها بنفسه في القنومية؛ وإن جاز ذلك جاز أن يكون وفاق الشيئين هو خلافهما وأن يكون.
Another question against the Melkites. It is said to them: Inform us about the essence which, according to you, is other than the hypostases: is it different from them or agreeing with them? If they say: It agrees with them, it is said to them: Then it must be [like] hypostases similar to them, and the essence must be a son inasmuch as it agrees with the Son, and a spirit inasmuch as it agrees with the Spirit, and it must be a hypostasis and a property for another fifth essence just as the hypostases are properties for an essence, and it must also be that its self is diversified inasmuch as it resembles diverse meanings and that it is the son of itself because it is like its Son and its Spirit and in their meaning; and this is great ignorance and abandonment of their statement that the meaning is different from what they came to. And if they say: The essence does not agree with the hypostases in every respect, but rather agrees with them in essentiality because their essence is from its essence, and differs from them in hypostaticity, it is said to them: Then the respect in which it agrees with them, namely essentiality, is the same respect in which it differs from them, namely hypostaticity; if they say yes, they make the meaning of essentiality the meaning of hypostaticity, and it is said to them: Then what prevents you from saying that the essence is a hypostasis for another essence and for itself? That would be abandoning their statement. If they say: The respect of difference between them, which is hypostaticity, is other than the respect of agreement, which is essentiality, it is said to them: Then there must be a fixed difference between the essence and the hypostases in hypostaticity, and that difference must not be other than either essence or accident, otherwise it would be necessary that it agrees with them by its own self in essentiality and differs from them by its own self in hypostaticity; and if that is allowed, it would be permissible that the agreement of two things is their difference and that...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of the Melkite Christian doctrine that distinguishes between the divine essence (جوهر) and the three hypostases (أقانيم: Father, Son, Holy Spirit). Baqillani poses a dilemma: either the essence agrees wholly with the hypostases or not. If it agrees wholly, then the essence itself must become a son, spirit, and a fourth hypostasis, leading to an infinite regress. If it agrees only in essence but differs in hypostaticity, then the same attribute is both agreeing and differing, which is contradictory. If they try to separate the respects, then the difference between essence and hypostases must be either essence or accident, which cannot be. Throughout, he shows that their distinction collapses into absurdity.

Key Terms
الجوهر
الأقانيم
القنومية
الجوهرية
الملكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Melkite distinction between essence and hypostases is a coherent metaphysical doctrine.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the distinction leads to logical contradictions, whether the essence is fully identical or partially distinct from the hypostases.

Checkpoint
What is the first alternative Baqillani considers about the essence and the hypostases?
A) The essence is completely different from the hypostases.
B) The essence is in agreement with the hypostases.
C) The essence is a fifth hypostasis.
D) The essence is composed of the three hypostases.

Key Takeaway
The Melkite distinction between essence and hypostases collapses because it leads to either infinite regress or self-contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

This passage exposes how even the smallest separation leads to absurdity. What concrete step will you take today to reinforce the absolute oneness of Allah in your worship and thoughts?
?
Baqillani forces the Melkites into a logical dead end because they tried to mix reason with revelation in a corrupted way. Does your own faith ever try to 'balance' Islamic monotheism with human logic in a way that compromises tawhid? Commit to seeking knowledge that protects your creed from such innovations, and name one source you will study to strengthen your aqeedah.

Absurdities of Full Agreement Between Substance and Hypostases
Baqillani enumerates absurdities following from full agreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a reductio argument to show that claiming the divine substance fully agrees with the hypostases leads to logical absurdities.

Core Idea
If the substance fully agrees with the hypostases, it becomes identical to them and even its own son.

This passage opens Baqillani's refutation of a Christian theological claim that the one divine substance is related to the three hypostases (Father, Son, Spirit) without being identical. Here he draws out the unacceptable consequences if the agreement is taken as complete. Prepare to see a cascade of contradictions that reveal the incoherence of the position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the flow of Baqillani's argument.
Note the repetitive structure: 'it must be that...'
2
Identify the absurd consequences listed
Baqillani lists several necessary consequences of full agreement. List each one as you find it.
Look for phrases like 'أن يكون الجوهر ابناً' (the substance is a son).
3
Understand the final absurdity
The climax is that the substance would be its own son and spirit, which is self-contradictory.
Baqillani calls this 'great ignorance'.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical force
Consider why Baqillani presents these consequences without yet addressing potential counterarguments. He aims to show the initial claim is untenable on its own terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيجب أن يكون أقانيم مثلها، وأن يكون الجوهر ابناً من حيث وافق الابن، وأن يكون روحاً من حيث وافق الروح، وأن يكون أقنوماً، وخاصاً لجوهر آخر خامس كما أن الأقانيم خواص لجوهر ويجب أيضاً أن تكون نفسه متباينة من حيث أشبهت أقانيم مختلفة المعاني وأن يكون ابن نفسه نفسه لأنه مثل ابنه وروحه وبمعناهما؛ وهذا جهل عظيم وترك لقولهم إن المعنى وروح مختلفة صاروا إليه.
وإن قالوا: ليس الجوهر موافقاً للأقانيم من كل جهة، وإنما يوافقها بالجوهرية لأن جوهرها من جوهره وإنما يخالفها في القنومية، قيل لهم: فالجهة التي وافقها بها وهي الجوهرية هي الجهة التي خالفها بها وهي القنومية؛ فإن قالوا نعم جعلوا معنى الجوهرية هو معنى القنومية، وقيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أن يكون الجوهر أقنوماً لجوهر آخر ولنفسه؟ وذلك ترك قولهم.
So it must be that He (the substance) is hypostases like them, and that the substance is a son inasmuch as it agrees with the Son, and a spirit inasmuch as it agrees with the Spirit, and a hypostasis, and a property of a fifth other substance just as the hypostases are properties of a substance. And it must also be that He Himself is diverse inasmuch as He resembles hypostases of different meanings, and that He is His own son because He is like His Son and His Spirit and in their meaning. This is great ignorance and abandonment of their statement that the meaning and spirit are different, to which they resorted. And if they say: The substance does not agree with the hypostases in every respect, but agrees with them in substantiality (jawhariyya) because their substance is from His substance, and differs from them in hypostaticity (qunumiyya), it is said to them: The respect in which it agrees with them, which is substantiality, is the respect in which it differs from them, which is hypostaticity. If they say yes, they make the meaning of substantiality the meaning of hypostaticity, and it is said to them: What prevents you from saying that the substance is a hypostasis for another and for itself? That would be abandonment of their statement.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian claim that the one divine substance (jawhar) is somehow related to the three hypostases (aqānīm) without being identical to them. Baqillani begins by drawing out the logical consequences of their position: if the substance must be like the hypostases, then it must itself be a hypostasis, and even a property of another substance, leading to infinite regress or absurdities like being its own son. He then considers the objection that the substance agrees only in substantiality but differs in hypostaticity. He counters that if the respects of agreement and difference are the same (both being the substance itself), then the distinction collapses, making substantiality and hypostaticity identical. This forces the Christian to admit that the substance is a hypostasis for another and for itself, which contradicts their own doctrine.

Key Terms
جوهر
أقنوم
أقانيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that claiming the substance agrees with the hypostases is a harmless theological statement.
Correction: Baqillani shows it leads to logical absurdities such as the substance being its own son, making the position untenable.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an absurd consequence Baqillani derives from full agreement?
A) The substance becomes a hypostasis.
B) The substance becomes a property of a fifth substance.
C) The substance becomes a property of itself.
D) The substance becomes its own son.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's first reductio shows that full agreement between substance and hypostases collapses into self-contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani forces us to confront logical absurdity in theology. When you hold beliefs about God, do you ever accept logical contradictions as 'mystery' without examining them? How does this lesson challenge you to think more rigorously about your own understanding of God's unity?
?
The substance becomes 'its own son'—an impossibility. Are there aspects of your faith where you have settled for comfortable but incoherent explanations just because they are familiar? What would it cost you to pursue logical coherence like Baqillani?
?
Baqillani points out that the Christians abandoned their own distinction between meaning and spirit. In your spiritual life, do you ever hold contradictory views about God's attributes—claiming He is one but then thinking of Him as composed? How can you ensure your worship is directed to the truly One God without compromise?

Collapse of the Partial Agreement Distinction
Baqillani refutes the partial agreement objection by equating agreement and difference respects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Christian attempt to limit agreement to substantiality alone by showing it makes substantiality and hypostaticity identical.

Core Idea
If the substance agrees in substantiality but differs in hypostaticity, the respects collapse into one meaning.

The Christian interlocutor might retreat to a partial agreement claim: the substance agrees with the hypostases only in 'substantiality' (jawhariyya) but differs in 'hypostaticity' (qunumiyya). Baqillani now turns this defense on its head. He shows that since both agreement and difference are attributed to the same substance, the distinction becomes meaningless.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Baqillani's response
Read the Arabic and translation to see the structure: objection, then counter-argument.
Notice the shift from the first reductio to a dialectical exchange.
2
Analyze the logic of the counter-argument
Baqillani argues that the respect of agreement (substantiality) cannot be different from the respect of difference (hypostaticity) if both refer to the same substance.
He uses a question: 'فالجهة التي وافقها بها هي الجهة التي خالفها بها' (the respect in which it agrees is the respect in which it differs).
3
Understand the final conclusion
If they concede, they make substantiality and hypostaticity the same, leading to the substance being a hypostasis for itself and another.
This would abandon their entire doctrine of distinct hypostases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So it must be that He (the substance) is hypostases like them, and that the substance is a son inasmuch as it agrees with the Son, and a spirit inasmuch as it agrees with the Spirit, and a hypostasis, and a property of a fifth other substance just as the hypostases are properties of a substance. If they say yes, they make the meaning of substantiality the meaning of hypostaticity, and it is said to them: What prevents you from saying that the substance is a hypostasis for another and for itself? That would be abandonment of their statement.

This passage is a refutation of the Christian claim that the one divine substance (jawhar) is somehow related to the three hypostases (aqānīm) without being identical to them. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'agreement in substantiality but difference in hypostaticity' is a coherent distinction.
Correction: Baqillani shows that because both are properties of the same substance, the distinction collapses into identity.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue follows from the Christian claim of agreement in substantiality but difference in hypostaticity?
A) The substance must be a fourth hypostasis.
B) The respects of agreement and difference become identical.
C) The substance becomes identical to each hypostasis separately.
D) The hypostases become properties of the substance.

Key Takeaway
The attempted escape to partial agreement fails because it makes substantiality and hypostaticity indistinguishable.

Responding to the Second Objection: Distinct Respects and the Christian Creed
Baqillani refutes the objection of distinct respects and cites the Nicene Creed as a demonstration of incoherence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that claiming distinct respects for agreement and difference leads to absurdity, and how he uses the Christian creed to illustrate its incoherence.

Core Idea
Distinct respects cannot avoid contradiction; difference must be a real attribute.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses the Christian objection that the respects of agreement (substantiality) and difference (hypostaticity) are distinct. He argues that this distinction itself requires the difference to be a substance or accident, otherwise the same entity would both agree and differ in the same respect. He then cites the Nicene Creed to highlight the contradictions in Christian beliefs, concluding that such incoherence proves their falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Baqillani's response
First, read the opening objection: 'If they say: The respect of difference... is other than the respect of agreement... it is said to them: So there must be a fixed difference...' Understand the logical structure.
Notice the conditional form of the objection.
2
Follow the logical argument
Notice that Baqillani demands that the difference must be either a substance or an accident. If not, the entity itself would both agree and differ, which is absurd.
He reduces their position to a contradiction.
3
Examine the cited creed
Read the long creed passage. Observe the claims about Jesus, the Trinity, incarnation, etc.
These are presented as examples of irrational beliefs.
4
Connect the creed to the argument
Baqillani presents the creed as an example of the absurdity, concluding that its contradictions are evidence against their position.
The creed's internal incoherence mirrors the logical flaw.

Source Text

He sees and what is seen? By the one only Son Jesus Christ, the Son of God, the only begotten, the firstborn of all creation, who was born of His Father before all worlds and not made, true God from true God, of the substance of His Father, by whom the worlds were established and all things were created for us, and for the sake of mankind and for our salvation He came down from heaven and was incarnate by the Holy Spirit and became man, and was conceived and born of the Virgin Mary, and was killed and crucified under Pontius Pilate and buried, then rose on the third day, and ascended to heaven and sits at the right hand of His Father, and is ready to come again to judge the living and the dead. Commentary
This passage continues the refutation. The Christians object that the respects of agreement (substantiality) and difference (hypostaticity) are distinct. He then cites the Nicene Creed as an example of the incoherent beliefs Christians hold, such as the incarnation and crucifixion of God. He concludes that the internal contradictions in their doctrines are proof of their falsehood.

Refuting Two Views on the Meaning of Hypostases
Baqillani refutes two Christian views on hypostases using logical reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutations of two Christian interpretations of the hypostases (attributes of substance vs. self-subsisting properties) and see how each leads to logical absurdities.

Core Idea
The hypostases cannot be attributes of a substance nor properties of themselves without breaking the Trinity.

Baqillani engages in interfaith theological debate by critiquing Christian doctrines of the Trinity. He presents two views on the nature of the hypostases (أقانيم) and demonstrates their internal inconsistencies. This passage shows the use of rational argument to expose contradictions in opposing beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own reasoning come through before you interpret.
Notice the two distinct views being addressed.
2
Identify the first view and its refutation
The passage first presents the view that hypostases are attributes of the substance. Find where Baqillani states this and how he argues against it.
He concludes this leads to affirming four entities, abandoning the Trinity.
3
Identify the second view and its refutation
The passage then presents the view that hypostases are self-subsisting properties. Find the argument and the absurd consequences Baqillani points out.
He shows the Son would be his own son, and the substance would be annulled.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider why both views are unacceptable from a Christian perspective. Baqillani uses logic to show they contradict the Trinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر اختلافهم في معنى الأقانيم زعم قوم منهم معنى الأقانيم التي هي الخواص أنها صفات للجوهر، فيقال لهم : إذا استحال أن تكون أقانيم وخواص لأنفسها وإنما تكون صفات وأقانيم لشيء آخر هو غيرها ولا يقال إنه هي فهذا يوجب إثبات أربعة معانٍ منها جوهر وثلاث خواص له وهذا ترك التثليث وإن قالوا : هي خواص لأنفسها وأقانيم لأنفسها قيل لهم : فيجب أن يكون الابن ابن نفسه والروح روح نفسه والصفة صفة نفسها وهذا جهل عظيم ويجب بطلان ما هي خواص له ونفيه وألا يكون هناك مخصوص بهذه الخواص وهذا إبطال للجوهر .
Mention of their disagreement on the meaning of the hypostases. A group of them claimed that the meaning of the hypostases which are the properties is that they are attributes of the substance. So it is said to them: 'If it is impossible for hypostases and properties to be for themselves, and they are only attributes and hypostases for something else that is other than them, and it is not said that it is them, then this necessitates affirming four entities: a substance and three properties for it, and this is abandonment of the Trinity.' And if they say: 'They are properties for themselves and hypostases for themselves,' it is said to them: 'Then the Son must be his own son, and the Spirit his own spirit, and the attribute its own attribute, and this is great ignorance. And it must be that the thing for which they are properties is annulled and negated, and that there is no thing specified by these properties, and this is an annulment of the substance.'
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two Christian views on the hypostases (أقانيم). First, some say the hypostases are attributes of the substance. Baqillani argues that if they are attributes of something else, then we have four distinct entities: the substance plus three attributes, which contradicts the Trinity (three in one). Second, others say the hypostases are properties of themselves (i.e., each hypostasis is its own property). Baqillani points out the absurd consequences: the Son would be his own son, the Spirit his own spirit, etc., which is nonsense. Moreover, if each hypostasis is a property of itself, then there is no underlying substance that possesses them, which effectively annuls the substance altogether. The passage does not complete the refutation of the third view (that they are persons/اشخاص) because the page ends.

Misconception: Baqillani is defending the Trinity.
Correction: Baqillani is attacking Christian formulations for being self-contradictory, not defending the Trinity.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani say is the consequence of claiming the hypostases are attributes of the substance?
A) It leads to pantheism.
B) It implies four entities, abandoning the Trinity.
C) It makes the Son equal to the Father.
D) It denies the divinity of Christ.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes two Christian interpretations of hypostases by exposing logical contradictions, showing they either multiply entities or cancel the substance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Both Christian views ultimately fail because they either multiply entities or annihilate the substance. Refutation of Hypostases as Attributes
Baqillani refutes the view that hypostases are attributes of the substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the Christian concept of hypostases as attributes of the divine substance.

Core Idea
The hypostases cannot be attributes without undermining the Trinity or reason itself.

Baqillani engages with Christian theology to expose an internal contradiction. If the hypostases are attributes of the divine substance, they become distinct entities, multiplying the divine. If they are self-attributes, they become self-referential absurdities. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the two conditional statements: 'if it is impossible...' and 'if they say...'.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Baqillani presents two possibilities: either the hypostases are attributes of something other than themselves, or they are attributes of themselves. Identify both.
3
Understand the consequences
For each scenario, trace the logical consequence: first leads to four eternal entities, second leads to self-reference and nullification of substance.
Reflect on why each consequence is unacceptable from a Christian perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر اختلافهم في معنى الأقانيم. زعم قوم منهم أن معنى الأقانيم التي للجوهر هي الخواص وأنها صفات، فيقال لهم: إذا استحال أن تكون أقانيم وخواص لأنفسها وإنما تكون صفات وأقانيم لشيء آخر هو غيرها ولا يقال إنه هي، فهذا يوجب إثبات أربعة معانٍ منها جوهر وثلاث خواص له، وهذا ترك التثليث. وإن قالوا: هي خواص لأنفسها وأقانيم لأنفسها، قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون الابن ابن نفسه والروح روح نفسه والصفة صفة نفسها، وهذا جهل عظيم، ويجب بطلان ما هي خواص له ونفيه، وألا يكون هناك مخصوص بهذه الخواص، وهذا إبطال للجوهر.
Section on mentioning their disagreement regarding the meaning of the hypostases. Some of them claimed that the meaning of the hypostases that belong to the substance is the properties (khawāṣṣ) and that they are attributes. So it is said to them: If it is impossible for them to be hypostases and properties for themselves, and rather they are attributes and hypostases for something else which is other than them and it is not said that it is them, then this necessitates the affirmation of four meanings: a substance and three properties for it, and this is an abandonment of the Trinity. And if they say: They are properties for themselves and hypostases for themselves, it is said to them: Then it must be that the Son is the son of himself, and the Spirit is the spirit of itself, and the attribute is the attribute of itself, and this is great ignorance, and it necessitates the nullification and negation of that for which they are properties, and that there be no entity specified by these properties, and this is an invalidation of the substance.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian interpretation of the hypostases (aqānīm) as properties (khawāṣṣ) or attributes (ṣifāt) of the divine substance. The author presents two alternative scenarios and shows that both lead to contradictions. First, if the hypostases are attributes of something else (the substance), then that something else is distinct from them, resulting in four eternal entities: the substance plus the three attributes. This contradicts the Trinity. Second, if they claim the hypostases are attributes of themselves, then each would be self-referential: the Son would be son of himself, etc., which is absurd. Furthermore, if they are self-attributes, the entity they supposedly qualify would be negated, destroying the substance itself. The argument thus forces the opponent into either polytheism or logical nonsense.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Baqillani is merely rejecting Christian terminology without engaging with the underlying logic.
Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that the hypostases-as-attributes doctrine is internally inconsistent, leading to either a quaternity or self-referential nonsense.

Checkpoint

?

If you are not equipped with such tools, what are you relying on to guard your creed? Will you commit to learning the logical foundations of your faith?

Refutation of Hypostases as Persons
Baqillani refutes the view that hypostases are persons, with a further objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the Christian interpretation of hypostases as persons or properties, and why it leads to inconsistency.

Core Idea
Hypostases cannot be persons or properties without undermining the Trinity.

Baqillani engages in a sophisticated dialectical argument against Christian theologians. He presents a dilemma: if the hypostases are persons, either they are independent or dependent on a substance—both problematic. Similarly, if they are properties, the same dilemma applies. This lesson walks through his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim
The passage begins by stating the Christian claim that hypostases are persons. Recognize the starting point of the argument.
2
First dilemma: persons
Baqillani asks whether these persons are self-subsistent or subsist in a common substance. Consider each horn of the dilemma.
If they are for themselves, they are independent, breaking unity. If they subsist in a substance, the substance is distinct, compromising the Trinity.
3
Second dilemma: properties
A variant claim says hypostases are merely properties. The same question applies: are they self-subsistent or dependent?
The same reasoning invalidates this claim as well.
4
Conclusion
Note that the same argument used against the persons-and-attributes view works here, and the opponents have no answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَزَعَمَ قوم منهم أن معنى الأقانيم والخواص أنها أشخاص فيقال لهم : أهي أشخاص لأنفسها أم لجوهر يجمعها؟ فإن قالوا : لأنفسها تركوا قولهم، وإن قالوا : لجوهر جامع لها أبطلوا التثليث . وقال بعضهم : معنى الأقانيم أنها خواص فقط فيقال لهم : أهي خواص لأنفسها أم لجوهر جامع لها هي خواص له. ويكلمون في ذلك بما كلمنا به من زعم أنها أشخاص وصفات، ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك .
And some of them claimed that the meaning of the hypostases and properties is that they are persons. So it is said to them: Are they persons for themselves or for a substance that encompasses them? If they say: For themselves, they abandon their statement; and if they say: For a substance that encompasses them, they invalidate the Trinity. And some of them said: The meaning of the hypostases is only properties. So it is said to them: Are they properties for themselves or for a substance that encompasses them, for which they are properties? And they are addressed in that with what we addressed those who claimed that they are persons and attributes, and they have no answer to that.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents two objections against Christian interpretations. First, if the hypostases are persons (ashkhāṣ), they must either be self-subsistent persons or persons subsisting in a common substance. If self-subsistent, then each is independent, which abandons the unity of God. If they subsist in a substance, then the substance is distinct from them, again compromising the Trinity. Second, some Christians say hypostases are only properties (khawāṣṣ). The same dilemma applies: are these properties self-subsistent or dependent on a substance? Either way leads to inconsistency. The author notes that the same line of argument used against the persons-and-attributes view applies here, and the opponents have no response.

Key Terms
أشخاص
خواص
جوهر جامع
تثليث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Christian doctrine is consistent because 'persons' implies relationship, but Baqillani's logical dichotomy shows it is not.
Correction: The dilemma of self-subsistence vs. dependence exposes a logical flaw: either the persons are independent entities (polytheism) or they depend on a substance that is not themselves (undermining the Trinity).

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what happens if Christians claim the hypostases are persons for themselves?
A) They preserve the Trinity
B) They abandon their own statement
C) They affirm a common substance
D) They invalidate the divinity of Christ

Key Takeaway
The Christian concept of hypostases as persons or properties cannot escape a logical contradiction, undermining its coherence.

?

Logical Argument on Fatherhood Distinction
Baqillani argues why the Father alone is Father, given shared substance and eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the Christian doctrine of Trinity leads to an arbitrary designation of the Father, given shared substance and co-eternality.

Core Idea
If all three hypostases are co-eternal and consubstantial, calling only one 'Father' is baseless.

Baqillani presents a logical challenge to the Christian notion of distinct personal properties within the Trinity. Assuming the hypostases share one substance and are all eternal, he questions what makes the first alone worthy of being called 'Father'. This passage sharpens the critique of arbitrary divine distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to understand the overall flow of Baqillani's reasoning.
Pay attention to the conditional starting with 'if'.
2
Identify the shared assumptions
Notice that Baqillani accepts the Christian claim that the hypostases share one substance and are co-eternal. This forms the basis of his argument.
He does not dispute these premises but uses them to expose inconsistency.
3
Trace the logical consequence
Follow how Baqillani concludes that if all are equally eternal and self-subsistent, there is no basis for singling out one as 'Father' rather than each being father to the others.
The conclusion is that the distinction is arbitrary and the opponents cannot justify it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى عليهم في الأقانيم. ويقال لهم: إذا كانت الأقانيم جوهراً واحداً وكان الأبُ جوهره جوهر الابن وجوهر الروح من جوهرهما، فلِمَ كان الابن والروح بأن يكونا ابناً وروحاً خاصين للأب أولى من أن يكون كل واحد منهما أباً؟ وأن يكون الأب خاصاً لهما، إذا كان الروح والابن جوهرين لأنفسهما، وكان جوهرهما من جوهر الأب، وكان الأب جوهراً لنفسه وكان قديماً لنفسه وكانا أيضاً قديمين لأنفسهما، ولم يكن الأب قبل الأقانيم والخواص ولا أسبق في الوجود ولا الخواص أسبقَ منه، فما الذي جعله بأن يكون أباً لهما أولى من أن يكون كل واحد منهما أباً لما جعلتموه أباً له، وأن يكون الأب خاصاً؟ فلا يجدون إلى تصحيح تحكمهم سبيلاً.
Another issue against them regarding the hypostases. And it is said to them: If the hypostases are one substance and the Father's substance is the substance of the Son and the substance of the Spirit is from their substance, then why is it that the Son and the Spirit are specifically son and spirit of the Father, rather than each of them being a father? And that the Father is specific to them, when the Spirit and the Son are substances for themselves, and their substance is from the substance of the Father, and the Father is a substance for himself and was eternal for himself, and they also are eternal for themselves, and the Father was not before the hypostases and properties nor prior in existence, nor are the properties prior to him, so what made it that He is a father to them rather than each of them being a father to that which you have made a father to him, and that the Father is specific? So they find no way to correct their arbitrary judgment.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents a logical argument against the distinct personal properties within the Trinity. The author assumes the Christian claim that the three hypostases share one substance and are co-eternal. If the Son and Spirit derive their substance from the Father, yet all are equally eternal and self-subsistent, the differentiation of Father, Son, and Spirit becomes arbitrary. Why should the first be called 'Father' rather than each being a father to the others? There is no temporal priority or essential distinction to ground the unique fatherhood of the first hypostasis. Thus, the Christian designation of the first as Father is an arbitrary stipulation without rational basis, and the opponents cannot justify it.

Key Terms
جوهر واحد
قديم

ابن

تحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Father's distinct role is based on being the source of the Son and Spirit.
Correction: Baqillani argues that if all are equally eternal and self-subsistent, sourcing does not justify unique fatherhood; the distinction remains arbitrary.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of Baqillani's argument in this passage?
A) The Son and Spirit are not divine
B) The Father's uniqueness cannot be justified if all hypostases are co-eternal and consubstantial
C) The Father created the Son and Spirit
D) The hypostases are not eternal

Key Takeaway
The Christian Trinity's personal properties lack rational grounding when substance and eternity are shared equally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a belief about Allah simply because it was taught to you, without ever subjecting it to the same logical scrutiny Baqillani applies here? Is there a belief you hold that you are afraid to examine rationally?
?
Baqillani exposes the 'arbitrary judgment' (تحكم) of the Christians. Where in your own life have you made arbitrary judgments about others—deciding they are 'wrong' or 'right' without evidence? How can you replace that with the demand for consistency and truth?
?
This passage shows that even theological claims must be logically coherent. If you were to apply this standard to your own understanding of Tawheed, what area might you find lacking? Are you ready to revise your views if they fail the test of reason?

Refutation of Christian Trinity: Persons or Properties
Baqillani refutes the Christian concept of persons (aqānīm) as independent or dependent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical dilemma against the Christian Trinity and how it applies to both persons and properties interpretations.

Core Idea
The Trinity collapses whether persons are independent or dependent.

Imam al-Baqillani presents a powerful logical argument against the Christian doctrine of the Trinity. He forces his opponents into a dilemma: if the three persons are independent, then there are three separate gods; if they depend on a single substance, then that substance is more fundamental than the persons. This passage applies the same reasoning to those who claim the persons are mere properties.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the logical structure become clear.
Notice that Baqillani uses a series of leading questions.
2
Identify the first dilemma
Find where Baqillani asks whether the persons are for themselves or for a substance. Understand how each option leads to a contradiction for Christians.
If persons are independent, they are multiple gods; if dependent, the substance is prior, negating co-eternality.
3
Understand the property interpretation
Some Christians said the persons are merely properties (khaṣā'iṣ). Baqillani applies the same dilemma to this view.
Properties must either be self-subsisting or inhere in a substance; both options again destroy the Trinity.
4
Conclude with Christian inability to answer
Baqillani asserts that Christians have no answer to this argument. Reflect on the strength of the logical refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهي شخاص لأنفسها أم لجوهر يجمعها؟ فإن قالوا : لأنفسها تركوا قولهم، وإن قالوا : لجوهر جامع لها أبطلوا التثليث. وقال بعضهم : معنى الأقانيم أنها خواص فقط فيقال لهم : أهي خواص لأنفسها أم لجوهر جامع لها هي خواص له. ويكلمون في ذلك بما كلمنا به من زعم أنها أشخاص وصفات، ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك.
Are they persons for themselves or for a substance that unites them? If they say: for themselves, they abandon their statement; and if they say: for a substance that encompasses them, they invalidate the Trinity. And some of them said: the meaning of the persons (aqānīm) is that they are only properties (khaṣā'iṣ). So it is said to them: Are they properties for themselves or for a substance that encompasses them, they being properties of it? And they are addressed in that with what we have addressed those who claim that they are persons and attributes, and they have no answer to that.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the Trinity. The author presents a dilemma: either the three persons (aqānīm) are independent entities in themselves, or they depend on a single underlying substance. If they are independent, this would mean three separate gods, undermining the Trinity; if they are dependent on a substance, that substance would be prior and the persons would be mere accidents, which also destroys the Trinity. Then some Christians claim the persons are merely properties (khaṣā'iṣ). The author applies the same dilemma: are these properties independent or dependent on a substance? Again, either way leads to contradiction. The author concludes that Christians cannot coherently defend their doctrine.

Key Terms
أقانيم
أشخاص
خواص
جوهر
تثليث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Baqillani is merely denying the Trinity without argument.
Correction: Baqillani actually provides a logical dilemma that exposes internal inconsistencies in Christian formulations.

Checkpoint
What is the first dilemma Baqillani presents to Christians about the persons (aqānīm)?
A) Whether they are created or uncreated.
B) Whether they are persons for themselves or for a substance that unites them.
C) Whether they are eternal or temporal.
D) Whether they are one or many.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's dilemma shows that the Christian concept of the Trinity is logically incoherent whether persons are considered independent entities or mere properties.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a religion claiming to worship one God yet describing three persons, does your heart immediately recoil with the clarity of tawhid, or do you feel a subtle pull toward intellectual compromise? How will you strengthen your conviction so that no ambiguity remains?
?
Baqillani exposed a logical dead end in the Trinity. Are there areas in your own understanding of Allah—perhaps concerning His attributes or actions—where you accept comfortable vagueness instead of seeking rigorous clarity? What step will you take this week to resolve one such ambiguity?
?
The Christians had no answer to Baqillani’s dilemma. If someone asked you a difficult question about your faith today, would you be able to give a clear, coherent response, or would you retreat into vague generalities? What will you commit to learning so that you can defend the truth with confidence?

Baqillani's Refutation: The Arbitrariness of the Trinity
Baqillani questions the basis for Trinitarian distinctions given shared essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument against the Trinity based on the shared essence and co-eternity of the persons, showing the arbitrariness of designating one as Father.

Core Idea
Shared essence and co-eternity make Trinitarian distinctions arbitrary.

This passage presents a second argument against the Christian Trinity. Baqillani assumes the persons share one substance and are co-eternal, then asks a simple question: if they are identical in essence and eternity, why is one called Father and another Son? He challenges Christians to justify this distinction without resorting to arbitrary claims. Let's read the passage and unpack his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow of the argument.
Notice the rhetorical questions that drive the argument.
2
Identify the premise
The premise is that the three persons are one substance (جوهر واحد) and co-eternal (قديم لنفسه).
3
Follow the question
Baqillani asks why the Son and Spirit are specifically related to the Father as son/spirit rather than each being a father. If all share the same essence, no one has priority.
4
Consider the implication
If no priority exists, the doctrine is arbitrary and cannot be rationally justified.
Christians have no way to justify their arbitrary judgment (تحكم).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى عليهم في الأقانيم. ويقال لهم : إذا كانت الأقانيم جوهراً واحداً وكان الأبُ جَوْهَرُه جَوْهَرِ الابْنِ وجوهر الروح من جوهرهما ، فلِمَ كان الابن والروح بأن يكونا ابناً وروحاً خاصين للأب أولى من أن يكون كل واحد منهما أباً؟ وأن يكون الأب خاصاً لهما، إذا كان الروح والابن جوهرين لأنفسهما، وكان جوهرهما من جوهر الأب، وكان الأب جوهراً لنفسه وكان قديماً لنفسه وكانا أيضاً قديمين لأنفسهما، ولم يكن الأب قبل الأقانيم والخواص ولا أسبق في الوجود ولا الخواص أسبقَ منه ، فما الذي جعله بأن يكون أباً لهما أولى من أن يكون كل واحد منهما أباً لما جعلتموه أباً له ، وأن يكون الأب خاصاً؟ فلا يجدون إلى تصحيح تحكمهم سبيلاً.
Another issue against them concerning the persons (aqānīm). And it is said to them: If the persons are one substance, and the Father's substance is the substance of the Son, and the substance of the Spirit is from their substance, then why are the Son and the Spirit such that they are son and spirit specifically for the Father, rather than each of them being a father? And why should the Father be specific to them, when the Spirit and the Son are substances for themselves, and their substance is from the substance of the Father, and the Father is a substance for Himself and is eternal in Himself, and they are also eternal in themselves, and the Father was not before the persons and the properties nor prior in existence, nor are the properties prior to Him? What made Him be a father to them rather than each of them being a father to what you make a father to Him, or the Father being specific? They will find no way to justify their arbitrary judgment.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument against the Trinity. Assuming the three persons (aqānīm) share one identical substance and are co-eternal, Baqillani asks why the Son and Spirit are specifically related to the Father as son and spirit, rather than each being a father to the other. If all are equally eternal and have the same substance, then no one deserves the title 'Father' over the others. The argument highlights the arbitrariness: why is one person the Father and another the Son? There is no basis in the shared essence. Therefore, Christians cannot rationally justify their doctrine.

Key Terms
أقانيم
جوهر
أب
ابن
روح
خاصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Baqillani misunderstands the Christian concept of eternal generation; rather, he shows that given shared essence, generation is arbitrary.
Correction: Baqillani's argument does not require a detailed understanding of eternal generation; it simply points out that if the essence is identical and all are co-eternal, there is no basis for one to be the source of the others.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue about the Father, Son, and Spirit if they share one substance and are co-eternal?
A) The Father must be prior in existence.
B) Each one has a different substance.
C) There is no reason for one to be Father and another Son.
D) The Spirit is not eternal.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's argument shows that the shared essence and co-eternity of the three persons make the Trinitarian distinctions arbitrary and indefensible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's oneness, do you ever subconsciously assign different roles or aspects to Him that seem in tension with each other? How does Baqillani's critique of arbitrary distinctions challenge you to examine any mental division of God's essence?
?
If you believe God is absolutely one, what in your life—your habits, your worship, your understanding of His attributes—might reflect a tendency to treat Him as composed of parts? Read the argument again and let it expose any hidden shirk in your thoughts.
?
Baqillani's argument leaves the Christians with 'no way to justify their arbitrary judgment.' How would you respond if you were in their place? Would you cling to a doctrine even if you couldn't defend it rationally? What does that reveal about your own attachment to beliefs?
